$V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, which is approximately 40 cm$^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $i$-th insertion, the number of balls inserted is $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $S_k = \sum_{i=1}^{k} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{k} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + \dots + 2^{k-1} = \frac{2^k - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^k - 1$.
The total volume of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $V_k = S_k \times V_{ball} = (2^k - 1) V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, $V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
From this, we can find the total volume of the stadium: $V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $n$ be the number of insertions required to fill the stadium.
Then, $V_n = (2^n - 1) V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$.
Substituting the expression for $V_{stadium}$:
$(2^n - 1) V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^n - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$.
$2^n - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$.
$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$.

We want to find how many insertions are *left* to fill it after the 30th insertion.
Since at the 30th insertion the stadium is half full, we need to fill the remaining half.
The volume of the remaining half is $V_{stadium} - V_{30} = V_{stadium} - \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium} = V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion. We are looking for the smallest integer $x$ such that the stadium becomes full.
If we perform one more insertion, i.e., the 31st insertion, the total volume of balls inserted will be $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2 + 1) V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} + 1 \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium} + V_{ball}$.
Since $V_{31} = V_{stadium} + V_{ball} > V_{stadium}$, the stadium will be filled (and even overfilled) after the 31st insertion.
Therefore, only one more insertion is needed after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium.

Number of insertions left = $31 - 30 = 1$.

Let $N_i$ be the number of golf balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion, where $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.

The total volume filled after $n$ insertions is $V_{filled}(n) = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, $V_{filled}(30) = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$, where $V_{stadium}$ is the total volume of the stadium.
From this, we can find the total volume of the stadium:
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find out how many more insertions are needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion. So, the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$.
The volume filled after $30 + x$ insertions is $V_{filled}(30+x) = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
We want to find the smallest integer $x$ such that $V_{filled}(30+x) \ge V_{stadium}$.
$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} \ge 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$

$2^{30+x} - 1 \ge 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 \ge 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} \ge 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} \ge 2^{31} - 1$

We need to find the smallest integer $x$ that satisfies this inequality.
If $x = 1$, then $2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
Is $2^{31} \ge 2^{31} - 1$ Yes, because $2^{31} - (2^{31} - 1) = 1 \ge 0$.
So, $x = 1$ is the smallest integer that satisfies the inequality.
Therefore, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Number of insertions left to fill it is 1.

$V_n = V_{stadium}$
$(2^n - 1) \times V_b = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_b$
$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$

$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31}$
$30+x = 31$
$x = 31 - 30 = 1$

So, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, which is approximately $40 cm^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
The number of balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion is $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is $T_k = \sum_{i=1}^{k} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{k} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + \dots + 2^{k-1} = \frac{2^k - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^k - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls after $k$ insertions is $V_k = T_k \times V_{ball} = (2^k - 1) V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So,
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
This implies that the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion. Then the total number of insertions needed to fill the stadium is $30 + x$.
The volume after $30 + x$ insertions should be equal to $V_{stadium}$.
$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$.
Substituting the value of $V_{stadium}$:
$(2^{30+x} - 1) V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We can approximate $2^{31} - 1 \approx 2^{31}$. So,
$2^{30+x} \approx 2^{31}$
$30+x \approx 31$
$x \approx 31 - 30 = 1$.

Let's check if $x=1$ is exactly correct or very close.
If $x=1$, total insertions are $30+1 = 31$.
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$.
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
We see that $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$ is slightly larger than $V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
However, the question asks how many insertions are *left* to fill it, meaning from the point when it is half full. Since the volume almost doubles with just one more insertion (from $2^{30}-1$ to $2^{31}-1$), and we are at half full at insertion 30, it will take only 1 more insertion to fill (and slightly overfill) the stadium.

Therefore, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_n$ be the total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions.
The number of balls inserted at the $k$-th insertion is $2^{k-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$N_n = \sum_{k=1}^{n} 2^{k-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2-1} = 2^n - 1$.
The volume of each golf ball is $v = 40 \text{cm}^3$.
So, the total volume of golf balls after $n$ insertions is $V_n = N_n \times v = (2^n - 1) \times 40 \text{cm}^3$.

Let $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So,
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times 40 = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times 40$.

Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely.
Then, after $30 + x$ insertions, the stadium will be full, i.e., $V_{30+x} = V_{stadium}$.
$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times 40 = V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times 40$.
Divide both sides by 40:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We need to find an integer $x$ that satisfies this equation or is the closest integer solution in the context of the problem.
Since $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate:
$2^{30+x} \approx 2^{31}$
$30+x \approx 31$
$x \approx 1$

Let's check if $x=1$ is the integer answer.
If $x=1$, the number of insertions left is 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, which is $40 cm^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $i$-th insertion, the number of balls inserted is $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted up to the $n$-th insertion is $S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \frac{1(2^n - 1)}{2-1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted up to the $n$-th insertion is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, $V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 V_{30} = 2 (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $n$ be the number of insertions required to fill the stadium. Then, the volume of balls inserted should be equal to the volume of the stadium:
$V_n = V_{stadium}$
$(2^n - 1) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$

We want to find how many more insertions are needed after the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$. We need to find $x$.
We are looking for an integer $x$ such that after $30+x$ insertions, the stadium is filled.
If we consider $x=1$, the total number of insertions is $30+1 = 31$.
The volume at 31st insertion is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$.
We compare $V_{31}$ with $V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
Since $2^{31} - 1 > 2^{31} - 2$, we have $V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is more than full. Since at 30 insertions it is half full, and with each insertion the volume approximately doubles, one more insertion will be enough to fill the stadium.

Number of additional insertions = $31 - 30 = 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_k$ be the total volume of golf balls inserted after $k$ insertions, and $V_s$ be the total volume of the stadium.
The number of balls inserted in the $n$-th insertion is $2^{n-1}$.
The volume of each golf ball is $v = 40 \text{cm}^3$.
The total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$$N_k = \sum_{i=1}^{k} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{k-1} = \frac{1 \cdot (2^k - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^k - 1$$
The total volume of golf balls after $k$ insertions is:
$$V_k = N_k \cdot v = (2^k - 1) \cdot v$$
At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So,
$$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v = \frac{1}{2} V_s$$
Thus, the full volume of the stadium is:
$$V_s = 2 \cdot V_{30} = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v$$
We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $n$ be the total number of insertions to fill the stadium. Then, the volume of golf balls should be equal to the volume of the stadium:
$$V_n = (2^n - 1) \cdot v = V_s$$
$$(2^n - 1) \cdot v = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v$$
Divide both sides by $v$:
$$2^n - 1 = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1)$$
$$2^n - 1 = 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2$$
$$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$$
$$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$$
$$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$$
We want to find the number of insertions *left* to fill it after the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then $n = 30 + x$.
$$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$$
Since $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate $2^{30+x} \approx 2^{31}$.
This gives $30+x \approx 31$, so $x \approx 1$.
Let's check for $x=1$, so $n=31$.
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \cdot v$.
$V_s = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v = (2^{31} - 2) \cdot v$.
$V_{31} - V_s = (2^{31} - 1) \cdot v - (2^{31} - 2) \cdot v = (2^{31} - 1 - 2^{31} + 2) \cdot v = 1 \cdot v = v$.
So, after 31 insertions, the volume is $V_s + v$, which is slightly more than full.
However, if we are looking for the number of insertions *left* to fill it, and at 30th insertion it is half full, then one more insertion will more than double the filled volume, hence it will fill the stadium.

Number of insertions left is 1.

Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball.
In the $i$-th insertion, $2^{i-1}$ golf balls are inserted.
The total number of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is given by the sum of a geometric series:
$N_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + 2^2 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = N_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $n_{full}$ be the number of insertions required to fill the stadium. Then the volume of golf balls at $n_{full}$ insertions should be equal to the stadium volume:
$V_{n_{full}} = (2^{n_{full}} - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$
Substituting the expression for $V_{stadium}$:
$(2^{n_{full}} - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{n_{full}} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{n_{full}} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{n_{full}} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{n_{full}} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{n_{full}} = 2^{31} - 1$

We want to find the number of insertions left to fill it after the 30th insertion. Let $k$ be the number of insertions left. Then $n_{full} = 30 + k$.
$2^{30+k} = 2^{31} - 1$
Since $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate $2^{30+k} \approx 2^{31}$, which gives $30+k \approx 31$, so $k \approx 1$.
Let's check if $k=1$ is the integer solution. If $k=1$, then $n_{full} = 31$.
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$

$V_{31} - V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball} - (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 1 - (2^{31} - 2)) \times V_{ball} = 1 \times V_{ball} = V_{ball} > 0$.
So after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfull. However, since at 30 insertions it is half full, and the number of balls approximately doubles with each insertion, it is reasonable to assume that just one more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Since we are asked for the number of insertions *left* to fill it, and at 30th insertion it is half full, one more insertion will make it slightly more than full.  Given the exponential nature of the filling, and the closeness of $2^{31}-1$ to $2^{31}$, the integer number of insertions left is 1.

Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $n$-th insertion, the number of golf balls inserted is $2^{n-1}$.

$V_n = (1 \times V_{ball}) + (2 \times V_{ball}) + (4 \times V_{ball}) + \dots + (2^{n-1} \times V_{ball})$
$V_n = V_{ball} \times (1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1})$
The sum of the geometric series $1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1}$ is given by $\frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
So, $V_n = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$

$V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$

$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2 \times 2^{30} - 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We need to solve for $x$. We can observe that if $x=1$, then $30+x = 31$, and we have $2^{31} - 1$ on the left side, which is very close to $2^{31}$.

So, $30+x = 31$, which gives $x = 31 - 30 = 1$.

Therefore, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

This is a geometric series with first term $a=1$, common ratio $r=2$, and number of terms $n=30$.
The sum of this geometric series is given by $S_n = \frac{a(r^n - 1)}{r - 1}$.
$N_{30} = \frac{1(2^{30} - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^{30} - 1$.

$2^k - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^k = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^k = 2^{31} - 1$.

$V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
This means that the stadium is filled during the 31st insertion.
Since we are already at the 30th insertion, we need $31 - 30 = 1$ more insertion to fill the stadium.

Number of insertions left to fill it = Total insertions to fill - insertions already done = $k - 30$.
Since $k=31$, the number of insertions left is $31 - 30 = 1$.

The total volume of golf balls inserted after n insertions is:
V_n = N_n * v = (2^n - 1) * v.

V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) * v = V / 2.

V = 2 * V_{30} = 2 * (2^{30} - 1) * v = (2 * 2^{30} - 2) * v = (2^{31} - 2) * v.

Substitute the expression for V:
(2^m - 1) * v = (2^{31} - 2) * v.
Divide both sides by v:
2^m - 1 = 2^{31} - 2.
Add 1 to both sides:
2^m = 2^{31} - 2 + 1.
2^m = 2^{31} - 1.

Since at 30th insertion it is half full, and at 31st insertion it is more than full, it means that exactly one more insertion is needed to fill the stadium after the 30th insertion.

Comparing $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$ with $V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$, we see that $V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled.
However, we are asked for the number of insertions *left* to fill it, implying the minimum number of additional insertions to reach at least full capacity. Since at 30 insertions it's half full, and at 31 insertions it's over full, it means we need just 1 more insertion to fill it.

Number of insertions left = $n_{full} - 30 = 31 - 30 = 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, $V_{ball} = 40 cm^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $n$-th insertion, the number of balls inserted is $2^{n-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$N_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + \cdots + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = \frac{1 \cdot (2^n - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = N_n \cdot V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 V_{30} = 2 (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$.
The volume of balls after $30 + x$ insertions is $V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) V_{ball}$.
We want to find the smallest integer $x$ such that $V_{30+x} \ge V_{stadium}$.
$(2^{30+x} - 1) V_{ball} \ge 2 (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$ (since $V_{ball} > 0$):
$2^{30+x} - 1 \ge 2 (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 \ge 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} \ge 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} \ge 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 1$

Let's test $x = 1$:
$2^{30+1} = 2^{31} = 2 \cdot 2^{30}$
Is $2^{31} \ge 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 1$
$2 \cdot 2^{30} \ge 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 1$
This is true. So, $x=1$ is sufficient.

Let's test $x = 0$:
$2^{30+0} = 2^{30}$
Is $2^{30} \ge 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 1$
$2^{30} \ge 2^{31} - 1$
$1 \ge 2^{31} - 2^{30} = 2^{30} (2 - 1) = 2^{30}$
$1 \ge 2^{30}$
This is false. So, $x=0$ is not sufficient.

Thus, the smallest integer $x$ that satisfies the inequality is $x=1$.
Therefore, there is only 1 insertion left to fill the stadium.

$2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
Add 1 to both sides:
$2^N = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^N = 2^{31} - 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Let V be the total volume of the stadium.
Let $v$ be the volume of a single golf ball, $v = 40 cm^3$.
In each insertion, the number of golf balls inserted doubles.
In the 1st insertion, $2^{1-1} = 2^0 = 1$ ball is inserted.
In the 2nd insertion, $2^{2-1} = 2^1 = 2$ balls are inserted.
In the 3rd insertion, $2^{3-1} = 2^2 = 4$ balls are inserted.
...
In the n-th insertion, $2^{n-1}$ balls are inserted.

The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$S_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=0}^{n-1} 2^i = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.

The total volume occupied by golf balls after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times v = (2^n - 1) \times v$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, the volume occupied after 30 insertions is half of the total stadium volume V.
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times v = \frac{V}{2}$
Therefore, the total stadium volume is $V = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times v$.

We want to find out how many more insertions are needed to fill the stadium completely from the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$.
The volume occupied after $30 + x$ insertions should be equal to the total stadium volume V.
$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times v = V$
$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times v = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times v$

Divide both sides by $v$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2 \times 2^{30} - 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We can check for $x=1$:
$2^{30+1} - 1 = 2^{31} - 1$
This matches the right side of the equation.
Therefore, $x = 1$.

So, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

In the 31st insertion, we add $2^{31-1} = 2^{30}$ balls.
The volume added in the 31st insertion is $2^{30} \times v$.
The remaining volume to be filled after 30 insertions is $V - V_{30} = V - \frac{V}{2} = \frac{V}{2} = (2^{30} - 1) \times v$.
Since $2^{30} \times v > (2^{30} - 1) \times v$, the volume added in the 31st insertion is more than the remaining volume to be filled. Thus, 1 more insertion is sufficient to fill the stadium.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, and $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
The number of balls inserted in the $i$-th insertion is $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $k$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$S_k = \sum_{i=1}^k N_i = \sum_{i=1}^k 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{k-1} = \frac{2^k - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^k - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls after $k$ insertions is $V_k = S_k \times V_{ball} = (2^k - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So, the volume of golf balls after 30 insertions is half the volume of the stadium:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
From this, we can find the full volume of the stadium:
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $n$ be the number of insertions required to fill the stadium. Then the volume of golf balls after $n$ insertions must be equal to the volume of the stadium:
$V_n = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$.
$(2^n - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
Add 1 to both sides:
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$.

We can observe that if we increase the number of insertions by 1 from 30 to 31, we add $2^{30}$ balls in the 31st insertion.
The volume at 30th insertion is $(2^{30} - 1)V_{ball}$, which is half the stadium volume. The remaining volume to be filled is also $(2^{30} - 1)V_{ball}$.
In the 31st insertion, we add $2^{30}$ balls, which have a volume of $2^{30}V_{ball}$.
Since $2^{30}V_{ball} > (2^{30} - 1)V_{ball}$, the 31st insertion will be enough to fill the remaining volume and potentially overfill it.
To find the exact number of insertions needed to fill the stadium, we need to solve $2^n = 2^{31} - 1$.
However, we are looking for an integer number of insertions. If we check for $n=31$:
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
Since $V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$, we see that $V_{31} > V_{stadium}$. This means that the stadium is filled during the 31st insertion.
Since the stadium is half full at the 30th insertion, and gets full by the 31st insertion, the number of additional insertions required after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium is $31 - 30 = 1$.

$V_{30+k} = V_b (2^{30+k} - 1)$.
We set $V_{30+k} = V_s$:
$V_b (2^{30+k} - 1) = 2 V_b (2^{30} - 1)$.

$2^{30+k} - 1 = 2 (2^{30} - 1)$.
$2^{30+k} - 1 = 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2$.
$2^{30+k} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^{30+k} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.

$V_s = V_b (2^{31} - 2)$

Therefore, exactly 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
In the $i$-th insertion, $2^{i-1}$ golf balls are inserted.
The total number of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is given by the sum of a geometric series:
$S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$
The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, the volume of golf balls after 30 insertions is half of the stadium volume:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$
This implies that the full volume of the stadium is:
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$

$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$

$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$
$V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$
We see that $V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
However, $V_{31}$ is the first insertion number that makes the volume greater than or equal to $V_{stadium}$. Since at 30th insertion it was half full, and the number of balls doubles with each insertion, it is logical that just one more insertion will be enough to fill the stadium. Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?Rationale:
Let $V$ be the volume of the stadium and $v = 40 \text{cm}^3$ be the volume of a golf ball.
In the $n$-th insertion, $2^{n-1}$ golf balls are inserted.
After $n$ insertions, the total number of golf balls inserted is $S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times v = (2^n - 1) v$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full.
So, $V_{30} = \frac{1}{2} V$.
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) v = \frac{1}{2} V$.
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is $V = 2 V_{30} = 2 (2^{30} - 1) v = (2^{31} - 2) v$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $N$ be the total number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Then, the volume of golf balls inserted after $N$ insertions should be at least $V$.
$V_N = (2^N - 1) v \ge V = (2^{31} - 2) v$.
Dividing by $v$ (since $v > 0$), we get $2^N - 1 \ge 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^N \ge 2^{31} - 1$.
We want to find the smallest integer $N$ that satisfies this inequality.
If we choose $N = 31$, then $2^{31} \ge 2^{31} - 1$, which is true.
If we choose $N = 30$, then $2^{30} < 2^{31} - 1$, since $2^{31} - 1 - 2^{30} = 2^{30} - 1 > 0$.
So, the smallest integer $N$ that satisfies $2^N \ge 2^{31} - 1$ is $N = 31$.
Thus, 31 insertions are needed to fill the stadium.

We are asked how many insertions are left to fill it after the 30th insertion.
Since 31 insertions are needed in total to fill the stadium, and 30 insertions have already been made, the number of insertions left is $31 - 30 = 1$.

$S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} V_i = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + 2^2 + ... + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2-1} = 2^n - 1$.

Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a single golf ball, which is given as $40 cm^3$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $Volume_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times 40 cm^3$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium. Then, at the 30th insertion, the volume filled is $\frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.

$(2^N - 1) \times 40 cm^3 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times 40 cm^3$.

$2^N - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^N - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 1$

$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$.

The number of balls already in the stadium after 30 insertions is $2^{30} - 1$.
In the 31st insertion, we add $2^{30}$ balls, which is approximately double the number of balls already present.
If half the stadium is filled with $2^{30} - 1$ balls, then adding roughly $2^{30}$ more balls should fill the remaining half and possibly more.

Let's consider the remaining volume to be filled after the 30th insertion. Since the stadium is half full at the 30th insertion, the remaining volume is equal to the volume already filled, which is $Volume_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times 40 cm^3$.
In the 31st insertion, the volume added is $V_{31} = 2^{31-1} \times 40 cm^3 = 2^{30} \times 40 cm^3$.
Since $2^{30} > 2^{30} - 1$, the volume added in the 31st insertion is greater than the remaining volume.
Therefore, just one more insertion (the 31st insertion) is sufficient to fill the stadium.
The number of insertions left to fill it after the 30th insertion is 1.

$2^{30+k} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+k} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+k} = 2^{31} - 1$

$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$

$30 + x = 31$
$x = 31 - 30$
$x = 1$

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, and $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
The number of golf balls inserted in each insertion is a geometric progression:
Insertion 1: $2^0 = 1$ ball
Insertion 2: $2^1 = 2$ balls
Insertion 3: $2^2 = 4$ balls
...
Insertion n: $2^{n-1}$ balls

The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of this geometric series:
$S_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=0}^{n-1} 2^i = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.

The volume filled after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So, the volume filled after 30 insertions is half of the stadium's volume:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$
Therefore, the total volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.

We want to find out how many more insertions are needed to fill the stadium completely from the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$.
The volume filled after $30 + x$ insertions should be equal to the total volume of the stadium:
$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$
$(2^{30+x} - 1) V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

We want to find an integer $x$ that satisfies this equation. Let's test if $x=1$.
If $x=1$, then $30+x = 31$.
Volume after 31 insertions is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$.
Stadium volume is $V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$.
Comparing $V_{31}$ and $V_{stadium}$:
$V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$
$V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) V_{ball}$
Since $2^{31} - 1 > 2^{31} - 2$, we have $V_{31} > V_{stadium}$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled.
Since the stadium was half full at the 30th insertion, and overfull after the 31st, it means that just 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Therefore, the number of insertions left to fill the stadium is 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let V be the total volume of the stadium.
Let $V_n$ be the volume of golf balls inserted after n insertions.
The number of balls inserted in the k-th insertion is $2^{k-1}$.
The volume of each golf ball is 40 cm$^3$.
So, the volume of golf balls inserted in the k-th insertion is $2^{k-1} \times 40$ cm$^3$.
The total volume of golf balls inserted after n insertions is the sum of volumes from the first to the n-th insertion:
$V_n = \sum_{k=1}^{n} 2^{k-1} \times 40 = 40 \times \sum_{k=1}^{n} 2^{k-1} = 40 \times (1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1}) = 40 \times (2^n - 1)$ cm$^3$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full, so $V_{30} = V/2$.
$V_{30} = 40 \times (2^{30} - 1) = V/2$
So, $V = 2 \times 40 \times (2^{30} - 1) = 80 \times (2^{30} - 1)$ cm$^3$.

We want to find the number of insertions N required to fill the stadium completely, i.e., $V_N = V$.
$V_N = 40 \times (2^N - 1) = V = 80 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
Divide both sides by 40:
$2^N - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^N - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 1$

We want to find the number of insertions left after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium. Let this number be x. Then the total number of insertions is $N = 30 + x$.
We need to find x such that $2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$.
Since $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate $2^{30+x} \approx 2^{31}$, which gives $30+x \approx 31$, so $x \approx 1$.
Let's check for $x=1$. Total insertions $N = 30 + 1 = 31$.
Volume after 31 insertions $V_{31} = 40 \times (2^{31} - 1)$.
Stadium volume $V = 80 \times (2^{30} - 1) = 40 \times 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) = 40 \times (2^{31} - 2)$.
$V_{31} - V = 40 \times (2^{31} - 1) - 40 \times (2^{31} - 2) = 40 \times [(2^{31} - 1) - (2^{31} - 2)] = 40 \times (2^{31} - 1 - 2^{31} + 2) = 40 \times 1 = 40$ cm$^3$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is filled with an excess volume of 40 cm$^3$, which is exactly the volume of one golf ball.
Since at 30th insertion it is half full, and we are asked for insertions to fill it, and in the next insertion we add approximately the same volume as already present, 1 more insertion is the logical answer.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_n$ be the total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions.

...
Insertion n: $2^{n-1}$ balls

The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$N_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = \frac{1 \cdot (2^n - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$

The volume of each golf ball is $v = 40 cm^3$.
The total volume of golf balls after $n$ insertions is $V_n = N_n \cdot v = (2^n - 1) \cdot v$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$
$V_{stadium} = 2 \cdot V_{30} = 2 \cdot (2^{30} - 1) \cdot v = (2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2) \cdot v = (2^{31} - 2) \cdot v$

$V_{30+x} = V_{stadium}$

$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

Since $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate:
$2^{30+x} \approx 2^{31}$
$30+x \approx 31$
$x \approx 1$

Let's check if $x=1$ is the integer solution that makes sense in this context. If we add 1 more insertion, we go to the 31st insertion.

The stadium volume is $V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) \cdot v$.

$V_{31} - V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 1) \cdot v - (2^{31} - 2) \cdot v = (2^{31} - 1 - 2^{31} + 2) \cdot v = 1 \cdot v = v = 40 cm^3$.

So, after 31 insertions, the volume of golf balls is slightly more than the stadium volume by the volume of one golf ball. However, given the doubling nature, and that at 30th it is exactly half full, it is implied that the next insertion will take it to full or slightly over full. In the context of the question asking "how many insertions are left to fill it", and given the doubling at each step, it is most likely asking for the integer number of insertions. In this case, it is 1 more insertion to go from half full to full (or slightly over full).

$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$

$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

$2^{30+1} - 1 = 2^{31} - 1$.
This is very close to $2^{31} - 2$.

However, given the exponential growth, if it is half full at 30th insertion, it will become full in just one more insertion, because the number of balls added in the 31st insertion is $2^{30}$, which is much larger than the total number of balls already in the stadium at insertion 30, which is $2^{30}-1$.

Since $2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$, it is clear that $x=1$ is the closest integer solution.
If we consider $x=1$, then we need $30+1=31$ insertions in total. The number of additional insertions needed is $31 - 30 = 1$.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $i$-th insertion, the number of balls inserted is $2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted up to the $n$-th insertion is the sum of a geometric series:
$$ \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 2^0 + 2^1 + 2^2 + ... + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2-1} = 2^n - 1 $$
The total volume of balls inserted up to the $n$-th insertion is $(2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So, the volume of balls inserted after 30 insertions is half the stadium volume:
$$ (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium} $$
This means the full volume of the stadium is:
$$ V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} $$

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $N$ be the number of insertions required to fill the stadium. Then the total volume of balls inserted after $N$ insertions must be equal to $V_{stadium}$:
$$ (2^N - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium} $$
Substitute the expression for $V_{stadium}$:
$$ (2^N - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} $$
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$$ 2^N - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) $$
$$ 2^N - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2 $$
$$ 2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 2 $$
$$ 2^N = 2^{31} - 2 + 1 $$
$$ 2^N = 2^{31} - 1 $$
We want to find how many more insertions are left after the 30th insertion to fill it. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then $N = 30 + x$.
We need to find $x$ such that after $30+x$ insertions, the stadium is full.
We know that after 30 insertions, it is half full.
Let's see what happens after one more insertion, i.e., at the 31st insertion.
Volume after 31 insertions = $(2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times (2^{30} - 1) + 2 - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} + 1 \times V_{ball}$.
Since $V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$,
Volume after 31 insertions = $V_{stadium} + V_{ball}$.
This means that after the 31st insertion, the stadium is overfilled by the volume of one golf ball. Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?The volume of golf balls inserted in each insertion follows a geometric progression: 1, 2, 4, 8, ... , 2^(n-1) for the n-th insertion.
The total number of balls inserted after n insertions is the sum of this geometric series, which is given by:
S_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^(n-1) = 2^n - 1.

Let V_ball be the volume of a single golf ball (40 cm^3).
The total volume of balls after n insertions is V_n = S_n * V_ball = (2^n - 1) * V_ball.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let V_stadium be the total volume of the stadium.
V_30 = (2^30 - 1) * V_ball = 0.5 * V_stadium.
So, the full volume of the stadium is V_stadium = 2 * V_30 = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * V_ball.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let x be the number of additional insertions. Then the total number of insertions will be 30 + x.
The total volume of balls after (30 + x) insertions is V_(30+x) = (2^(30+x) - 1) * V_ball.
For the stadium to be full, we need V_(30+x) = V_stadium.
(2^(30+x) - 1) * V_ball = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * V_ball.
Divide both sides by V_ball:
2^(30+x) - 1 = 2 * (2^30 - 1)
2^(30+x) - 1 = 2 * 2^30 - 2
2^(30+x) = 2 * 2^30 - 2 + 1
2^(30+x) = 2 * 2^30 - 1
2^(30+x) = 2^(31) - 1

Let's check for x = 1:
2^(30+1) = 2^(31).
2^(31) and 2^(31) - 1 are very close for large numbers.
If x = 1, the total volume is V_(31) = (2^(31) - 1) * V_ball.
We know V_stadium = 2 * (2^30 - 1) * V_ball = (2^(31) - 2) * V_ball.

V_stadium = (2^(31) - 2) * V_ball

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?1?1?1?Let $V_i$ be the volume of golf balls after the $i$-th insertion.
The number of balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion is $2^{i-1}$.
The volume of each golf ball is $40 cm^3$.
The total volume of golf balls after $n$ insertions is given by the sum of volumes of balls inserted in each insertion from 1 to $n$:
$V_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} (2^{i-1} \times 40 cm^3) = 40 \times \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 40 \times (1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1})$
The sum of a geometric series $1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
So, $V_n = 40 \times (2^n - 1) cm^3$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let $V_{full}$ be the full volume of the stadium.
$V_{30} = 40 \times (2^{30} - 1) cm^3 = \frac{1}{2} V_{full}$
$V_{full} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times 40 \times (2^{30} - 1) cm^3 = 80 \times (2^{30} - 1) cm^3$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $n$ be the number of insertions required to fill the stadium completely.
$V_n = V_{full}$
$40 \times (2^n - 1) = 80 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
Divide both sides by 40:
$2^n - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^n - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^n - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^n = 2^{31} - 1$

$2^{30+m} = 2^{31} - 1$
Since $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$, we can approximate $2^{30+m} \approx 2^{31}$.
$30 + m \approx 31$
$m \approx 1$

Let's check if $m=1$. Number of additional insertions is 1.
Total insertions = $30 + 1 = 31$.
$V_{31} = 40 \times (2^{31} - 1) cm^3$
$V_{full} = 80 \times (2^{30} - 1) cm^3 = 40 \times 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) cm^3 = 40 \times (2^{31} - 2) cm^3$
$V_{31} - V_{full} = 40 \times (2^{31} - 1) - 40 \times (2^{31} - 2) = 40 \times [(2^{31} - 1) - (2^{31} - 2)] = 40 \times (2^{31} - 1 - 2^{31} + 2) = 40 \times 1 = 40 cm^3$.
$V_{31}$ is slightly larger than $V_{full}$ by exactly the volume of one golf ball.
Since at 30th insertion the stadium is half full, and we need to find how many more insertions are needed to fill it, and 1 more insertion makes it slightly overfull, and given the doubling nature, 1 is the most reasonable integer answer.

The volume filled after n insertions is V_n = T_n * v = (2^n - 1) * v.

V_30 = (2^30 - 1) * v = V / 2.

2^(30+k) - 1 = 2^31 - 2.
2^(30+k) = 2^31 - 2 + 1.
2^(30+k) = 2^31 - 1.

V_31 - V = (2^31 - 1) * v - (2^31 - 2) * v = (2^31 - 1 - (2^31 - 2)) * v = (2^31 - 1 - 2^31 + 2) * v = 1 * v = v.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, given as $40 \text{cm}^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
The number of balls inserted in each insertion follows a geometric progression:
Insertion 1: $2^{1-1} = 1$ ball
Insertion 2: $2^{2-1} = 2$ balls
Insertion 3: $2^{3-1} = 4$ balls
...
Insertion $n$: $2^{n-1}$ balls

The total number of balls inserted up to insertion $n$ is the sum of this geometric series:
$S_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$

The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So,
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$
This means the full volume of the stadium is $V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $N$ be the insertion number when the stadium is full. Then the volume of balls at insertion $N$ should be equal to $V_{stadium}$:
$V_N = (2^N - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$
$(2^N - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$

Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^N - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^N - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^N = 2^{31} - 1$

We want to find the number of insertions *left* to fill the stadium after the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then $N = 30 + x$.
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

Since $2^{31}$ is much larger than 1, $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$. For practical purposes, we can approximate $2^{31} - 1 \approx 2^{31}$.
So, $2^{30+x} \approx 2^{31}$
$30+x \approx 31$
$x \approx 31 - 30$
$x \approx 1$

Let's check if $x=1$ (meaning $N=31$) is the exact integer solution.
If $N = 31$, then $2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 1$.
And $2 \times (2^{30} - 1) = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^{31} - 1 \neq 2^{31} - 2$.
However, we are asked for the number of insertions left to fill it.
From insertion 30 to insertion 31, we need to add balls inserted at insertion 31 which is $2^{31-1} = 2^{30}$ balls.
The volume at insertion 30 is $(2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$. The volume required to fill is also $(2^{30} - 1) V_{ball}$.
In the 31st insertion we add $2^{30}$ balls. The volume added is $2^{30} V_{ball}$.
If we add the volume at insertion 30 with the volume added at insertion 31:
$(2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} + 2^{30} V_{ball} = (2^{30} - 1 + 2^{30}) V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 1) V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 1) V_{ball}$.
This is the volume at insertion 31.
So, exactly 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $n$-th insertion, the number of balls inserted is $2^{n-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$N_n = 1 + 2 + 4 + \cdots + 2^{n-1} = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = \frac{1(2^n - 1)}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $V_n = N_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So, the volume after 30 insertions is half of the stadium volume:
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is:
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of insertions required to fill the stadium completely. Let $N$ be the total number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Then the volume after $N$ insertions must be equal to the stadium volume:
$V_N = (2^N - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium}$.
$(2^N - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^N - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^N = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^N = 2^{31} - 1$.

We are asked for the number of insertions *left* to fill it after the 30th insertion. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions needed after the 30th insertion. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$. We need to find $x$ such that $N = 30 + x$.
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$.
If we approximate $2^{31} - 1 \approx 2^{31}$, then $2^{30+x} \approx 2^{31}$, which gives $30+x \approx 31$, so $x \approx 1$.

Let's check if $x=1$ (so total insertions = 31) is the correct answer.
For $N = 31$, the volume is $V_{31} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
We know $V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.
$V_{31} - V_{stadium} = (2^{31} - 1) \times V_{ball} - (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 1 - 2^{31} + 2) \times V_{ball} = 1 \times V_{ball} = V_{ball}$.
So $V_{31} = V_{stadium} + V_{ball}$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled by the volume of one golf ball. However, since at 30 insertions it is half full, one additional insertion should be sufficient to fill it to a very close to full state and even slightly overfill, which in practical terms means it is filled. Given the nature of exponential growth, going from half full to full in one step is expected in this doubling process.

Therefore, the number of insertions left to fill it is 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_n$ be the total volume occupied by the golf balls after $n$ insertions. The number of balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion is $2^{i-1}$, and each golf ball has a volume of $40 \text{cm}^3$.
So, the volume added at the $i$-th insertion is $2^{i-1} \times 40 \text{cm}^3$.
The total volume after $n$ insertions is the sum of the volumes added at each insertion from 1 to $n$:
$V_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} (2^{i-1} \times 40) = 40 \times \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 40 \times (1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1})$.
This is a geometric series with first term $a = 1$, common ratio $r = 2$, and $n$ terms. The sum of this geometric series is $\frac{r^n - 1}{r - 1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.
So, $V_n = 40 \times (2^n - 1)$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
$V_{30} = 40 \times (2^{30} - 1) = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
Therefore, $V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times 40 \times (2^{30} - 1) = 80 \times (2^{30} - 1)$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium. Let $k$ be the number of additional insertions. Then we will have a total of $30 + k$ insertions. We want to find the smallest integer $k$ such that $V_{30+k} \ge V_{stadium}$.
$V_{30+k} = 40 \times (2^{30+k} - 1)$.
We want to find $k$ such that $V_{30+k} \ge V_{stadium}$.
$40 \times (2^{30+k} - 1) \ge 80 \times (2^{30} - 1)$.
Divide both sides by 40:
$2^{30+k} - 1 \ge 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$.
$2^{30+k} - 1 \ge 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$.
$2^{30+k} - 1 \ge 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^{30+k} \ge 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^{30+k} \ge 2^{31} - 1$.

Let's check for $k=1$.
$2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
Is $2^{31} \ge 2^{31} - 1$ Yes, it is.
So, $k=1$ is sufficient.
Let's check for $k=0$.
$2^{30+0} = 2^{30}$.
Is $2^{30} \ge 2^{31} - 1$ No, because $2^{31} - 1 > 2^{30}$.
So, we need at least $k=1$ additional insertion.

Therefore, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V$ be the volume of the stadium and $v = 40 \text{cm}^3$ be the volume of a golf ball.
In the $n$-th insertion, the number of balls inserted is $2^{n-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of the geometric series:
$$ \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1 $$
The total volume of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $(2^n - 1)v$.

At the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. This means that the volume of golf balls after 30 insertions is $V/2$.
$$ (2^{30} - 1)v = \frac{V}{2} $$
So, the full volume of the stadium is $V = 2(2^{30} - 1)v$.

We want to find the number of insertions required to fill the stadium completely. Let $m$ be the total number of insertions needed to fill the stadium. Then the volume of golf balls after $m$ insertions must be equal to $V$.
$$ (2^m - 1)v = V $$
Substitute the expression for $V$ from the first equation:
$$ (2^m - 1)v = 2(2^{30} - 1)v $$
Divide both sides by $v$:
$$ 2^m - 1 = 2(2^{30} - 1) $$
$$ 2^m - 1 = 2 \cdot 2^{30} - 2 $$
$$ 2^m - 1 = 2^{31} - 2 $$
$$ 2^m = 2^{31} - 2 + 1 $$
$$ 2^m = 2^{31} - 1 $$
We want to find the number of insertions left to fill the stadium. We have already made 30 insertions. Let $k$ be the number of additional insertions needed. Then $m = 30 + k$.
We want to find $k = m - 30$.
From $2^m = 2^{31} - 1$, we can see that $m$ is very close to 31.

Since $2^{31} - 1$ is slightly less than $2^{31}$, $m$ is slightly less than 31. However, as the number of insertions must be an integer, let's consider the next integer value after 30.
If we consider $m = 31$, then the volume filled is $(2^{31} - 1)v$.
The stadium volume is $V = 2(2^{30} - 1)v = (2^{31} - 2)v$.
Comparing $(2^{31} - 1)v$ and $(2^{31} - 2)v$, we see that $(2^{31} - 1)v > (2^{31} - 2)v$.
This means that after 31 insertions, the stadium is slightly overfilled. However, we are asked for the number of insertions *left* to fill it, meaning from the 30th insertion onwards.

Since at the 30th insertion the stadium is half full, we need to fill the other half.
In the 31st insertion, we add $2^{30}$ balls.
The volume at 30th insertion is $(2^{30} - 1)v$.
The volume added in the 31st insertion is $2^{30}v$.
Since $2^{30}v$ is approximately equal to $(2^{30} - 1)v$, it is reasonable to assume that one more insertion will fill the remaining half.

Indeed, we see that to reach volume $V = 2(2^{30} - 1)v$, we need $m$ insertions such that $2^m - 1 = 2(2^{30} - 1) = 2^{31} - 2$.
So $2^m = 2^{31} - 1$.
Since $2^{30} < 2^{31} - 1 < 2^{31}$, we have $30 < m < 31$. However, $m$ must be an integer number of insertions.
If we consider that "fill it" likely means at least fill it, and we are asked for how many insertions are *left* to fill it *from the 30th insertion*, and we know that at 30 insertions it is half full, and the volume approximately doubles with each insertion, then just one more insertion should be enough to fill the remaining half.

The closest integer to $m$ such that $2^m = 2^{31} - 1$ is $m=31$.
If we take $m=31$, the stadium is filled with $(2^{31} - 1)v$, which is slightly more than required volume $V = (2^{31} - 2)v$.
Thus, 1 more insertion is needed to fill it.

Let $N_i$ be the number of balls inserted at the $i$-th insertion. We are given that $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.
The total number of balls inserted after $n$ insertions is $S_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + \dots + 2^{n-1} = 2^n - 1$.
The total volume occupied by the golf balls after $n$ insertions is $V_n = S_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. Let $V_{stadium}$ be the volume of the stadium.
So, $V_{30} = V_{stadium} / 2$.
$(2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = V_{stadium} / 2$.
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium completely. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions. Then the total number of insertions will be $30 + x$.
The volume occupied after $30+x$ insertions is $V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
We want $V_{30+x} = V_{stadium}$.
$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1)$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2 \times 2^{30} - 2$
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$

Let's think about the remaining volume after 30 insertions and the volume added in subsequent insertions.
After 30 insertions, the stadium is half full, so half of the stadium is empty.
Volume filled at 30th insertion is $V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
Remaining volume is $V_{stadium} / 2 = V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
Volume inserted in the 31st insertion is $N_{31} \times V_{ball} = 2^{31-1} \times V_{ball} = 2^{30} \times V_{ball}$.
Since $2^{30} > 2^{30} - 1$, the volume inserted in the 31st insertion is greater than the remaining volume. Thus, only 1 more insertion is needed to fill the stadium.

Number of insertions left = 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?Let $V_{ball}$ be the volume of a golf ball, $V_{ball} = 40 cm^3$.
Let $V_{stadium}$ be the total volume of the stadium.
In the $i$-th insertion, the number of golf balls inserted is $N_i = 2^{i-1}$.

The total number of golf balls inserted after $n$ insertions is the sum of a geometric series:
$Total\_balls_n = \sum_{i=1}^{n} N_i = \sum_{i=1}^{n} 2^{i-1} = 1 + 2 + 4 + ... + 2^{n-1} = \frac{2^n - 1}{2 - 1} = 2^n - 1$.

The volume occupied by golf balls after $n$ insertions is:
$V_n = Total\_balls_n \times V_{ball} = (2^n - 1) \times V_{ball}$.

We are given that at the 30th insertion, the stadium is exactly half full. So,
$V_{30} = (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = \frac{1}{2} V_{stadium}$.
Therefore, the full volume of the stadium is:
$V_{stadium} = 2 \times V_{30} = 2 \times (2^{30} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2 \times 2^{30} - 2) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.

We want to find the number of additional insertions needed to fill the stadium. Let $x$ be the number of additional insertions after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium. So, we are looking for the total number of insertions $30 + x$ such that the stadium is full.
The volume occupied after $30 + x$ insertions is:
$V_{30+x} = (2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball}$.
We want $V_{30+x} = V_{stadium}$.
$(2^{30+x} - 1) \times V_{ball} = (2^{31} - 2) \times V_{ball}$.
Divide both sides by $V_{ball}$:
$2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 2$.
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 2 + 1$.
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31} - 1$.

We need to find an integer $x$ that satisfies this equation.
Let's check for small integer values of $x$.
If $x = 1$, then $2^{30+1} = 2^{31}$.
$2^{31} = 2^{31} - 1 + 1$.
So, $2^{31} - 1$ is very close to $2^{31}$.
If $x = 1$, $2^{30+1} - 1 = 2^{31} - 1$.

So we need to solve $2^{30+x} - 1 = 2^{31} - 1$.
$2^{30+x} = 2^{31}$.
$30 + x = 31$.
$x = 31 - 30 = 1$.

So, we need 1 more insertion after the 30th insertion to fill the stadium.
The number of insertions left to fill it is 1.

Final Answer: The final answer is $\boxed{1}$?
